The genome annotation pipeline is presented in Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0271-y#MOESM1">2d</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec21">Gene family analysis</h3><p>The protein data of some representative plant species, including <i>A. thaliana</i>, <i>A. setaceus</i>, <i>A. officinalis</i>, <i>A. trichopoda</i>, <i>C. papaya</i>, <i>M. acuminate</i>, <i>O. sativa</i>, <i>P. dactylifera</i>, <i>P. equestris</i>, <i>P. trichocarpa</i>, <i>S. lycopersicum</i>, <i>S. oleracea</i>, and <i>V. vinifera</i>, were retrieved from the NCBI database and used for gene family clustering. All protein sequences were pooled and clustered into different kinds of homologs by using the software OrthoMCL with default parameter settings<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Li, L. Jr, Stoeckert, C. J. &amp; Roos, D. S. OrthoMCL: identification of ortholog groups for eukaryotic genomes. Genome Res. 13, 2178â2189 (2003)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0271-y#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d14961e1941">57</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec22">Phylogenetic tree reconstruction and divergence time prediction</h3><p>A total of 1002 single-copy genes shared by the analyzed genomes were used for subsequent phylogenetic tree building and divergence time evaluation. The selected protein sequences were concatenated and subjected to multiple alignments by using MAFFT<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Katoh, K. &amp; Standley, D. M. MAFFT multiple sequence alignment software version 7: improvements in performance and usability. Mol. Biol. Evol. 30, 772â780 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0271-y#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d14961e1953">58</a></sup>, and the less regions were filtered using Gblocks<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Castresana, J. Selection of conserved blocks from multiple alignments for their use in phylogenetic analysis. Mol. Biol. Evol. 17, 540â552 (2000)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0271-y#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d14961e1957">59</a></sup>. Then, a phylogenetic tree was constructed using RAxML<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Stamatakis, A. RAxML-VI-HPC: maximum likelihood-based phylogenetic analyses with thousands of taxa and mixed models. Bioinformatics 22, 2688â2690 (2006)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0271-y#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d14961e1961">60</a></sup>, and <i>A. trichopoda</i> was used as the root. The divergence time was estimated using MCMCtree, which was incorporated in the PAML package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Yang, Z. PAML: a program package for phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Comput. Appl. Biosci. 13, 555â556 (1997)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0271-y#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d14961e1968">61</a></sup>. The expansion and contraction of the gene family were analyzed with CAFE (v1.6)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="De Bie, T., Cristianini, N., Demuth, J. P. &amp; Hahn, M. W. CAFE: a computational tool for the study of gene family evolution. Bioinformatics 22, 1269â1271 (2006)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0271-y#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d14961e1973">62</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec23">Detection of polyploidization events</h3><p>To detect the polyploidization events in the <i>A. setaceus</i> genome, the protein sequences from <i>A. setaceus</i> were intercompared by using BLASTP (<i>E</i>-valueâ&lt;â1eâ05) to identify the conserved paralogs. Protein sequences of <i>P. dactylifera</i>, <i>V. vinifera</i>, and <i>P. equestris</i> were also analyzed, and used for comparison. Then, the WGD events of each species were estimated on the basis of the 4DTv and Ks distributions.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec24">Positively selected gene analysis</h3><p>To detect the positively selected genes in <i>A. setaceus</i>, the single-copy genes of <i>A. setaceus</i> and the closely related species <i>A. officinalis</i> were aligned using MUSCLE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Edgar, R. C. MUSCLE: multiple sequence alignment with high accuracy and high throughput. Nucleic Acids Res. 32, 1792â1797 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0271-y#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d14961e2022">63</a></sup>. Positive selection sites were detected with <i>A. setaceus</i> as a predetermined branch by using Codeml software (part of the PAML program package) with a branch-site model. The positively selected genes were annotated by GO and KEGG analyses.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec25">Identification of resistance (R) genes</h3><p>To identify R genes, the <i>A. setaceus</i> genome was queried with HMM search by using the HMM profile of the NB-ARC domain (Pfam accession number: PF00931). Then, the NBS domain of the candidate genes was confirmed using the NCBI Conserved Domain Database (CDD)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Marchler-Bauer, A. et al. CDD: NCBIâs conserved domain database. Nucleic Acids Res. 43, D222âD226 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0271-y#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d14961e2040">64</a></sup> and the Pfam database<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Finn, R. D. et al. Pfam: the protein families database. Nucleic Acids Res. 42, D222âD230 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0271-y#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d14961e2044">65</a></sup>. The genes without an NBS domain were removed. The confirmed genes belonging to different groups were classified based on the conserved domains that they encoded using the CDD and Pfam databases.</p></div></div></section>
                

                <section aria-labelledby="data-availability" data-title="Data availability"><div class="c-article-section" id="data-availability-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="data-availability">Data availability</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="data-availability-content">
              
              <p>Raw data from this study were deposited in the NCBI SRA (Sequence Read Archive) database under the Bioproject ID: <a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject/?term=PRJNA564485">PRJNA564485</a>. The genome sequence data (Nanopore, Illumina, 10Ã Genomics, and Hi-C data) are available under accession numbers SRR10176977, SRR10177257, SRR10176978, SRR10187020, and SRR10187021. Transcriptome data are available under accession numbers SRR10177390, SRR10177391, SRR10186988, and SRR10187001. The assembled genome sequences have been deposited at DDBJ/ENA/GenBank under the accession WHSE00000000. Gene models are available at Dryad (<a href="https://doi.org/10.5061/dryad.1c59zw3rm">https://doi.org/10.5061/dryad.1c59zw3rm</a>).</p>
